Said the author of this book when I completed for you, O children, this book which is a part of the science of medicine in its completeness and reached the goal in it from its clarity and explanation, I saw that I complete it for you with this article which is a part of working with the hand.
Because work by hand is perfected in our country and in our time it is completely absent, so that its science was almost studied and its trace cut off. And only what remains of it are slight drawings in the books of the ancients which my hands have corrected and made its errors and confusion, until its meanings were obscured and its benefit was lost.
So I saw that I revive it and compose in it this article on the path of explanation, clarification, and brevity, and to bring pictures of surgical instruments and all the tools of work since it is from the increase of explanation and from the aid of what is needed for it.
And the reason that there is no skillful maker with his hand in our time is because the craft of medicine is long and it befits its owner to practice beforehand in the science of anatomy which Galen described. Until he stands on the benefits of the organs, their systems, their temperaments, and their connection and separation, and knowledge of the bones, nerves, muscles, their number, exits, veins, arteries, and the places of their exits.
Therefore, Ibrāhīm said that physicians by name are many and in deed few, especially in the craft of the hand, and we mentioned from that a part in the introduction to this book.
Because he who is not knowledgeable about what we mentioned from anatomy, did not avoid falling into an error that kills people with it, as I have witnessed many who imagined themselves in this science and claimed it without knowledge or study.
And because I saw a ignorant physician who had cut into a boar's tumor in a woman's neck, and severed some of the neck's arteries so that the woman bled until she fell dead before his eyes.
I saw another physician who advanced in extracting a stone from a man who had been pierced in the bladder, and the stone was large, so he became terrified, and he extracted it with a piece of the bladder wall. And the man died after about three days, and I was summoned to extract it, and I saw from the size of the stone and the state of the sick person what I judged to be the case.
And I saw another physician who was making a living among some leaders in our country by practicing medicine.
So it happened to a young black boy who had a fracture in his leg near the heel with a wound, so the physician, out of ignorance, hurried and tightened the fracture on the wound with splints and bandages tightly, leaving no space for the wound to breathe.
Then he released him on his desires and left him for days, ordering him not to loosen the bandage until his leg and foot swelled and was close to death.
So I was summoned to him and quickly loosened the bandage, so he found relief and was freed from his pains except that the corruption had become firmly established in the limb, and I was unable to undo it.
So the corruption continued to spread in the limb until he died.
And I saw another physician who treated a cancerous tumor, so it recurred after days until it became a great affliction for its owner, because if cancer is pure from black humors, then it should not be exposed to iron at all.
Unless it is in a limb that can be entirely removed.
For this reason, my sons, it is necessary for you to learn that work with the hand is divided into two parts: work accompanied by safety and work that comes with harm in most cases.
And I have warned in every place that this book reaches, about work that involves danger and fear, so it is necessary for you to avoid them and refuse them.
Lest the ignorant find a way to speak and criticize, take for yourselves firmness and caution, and in dealing with them be characterized by kindness and steadiness.
And employ the best path leading to safety and a praiseworthy outcome, and beware of dangerous and difficult illnesses.
And keep yourselves away from what you fear might cause doubt to enter upon you in your religion and worldly affairs, for it is more beneficial for your standing and higher in this world and the next for your destinies.
For Galen said in some of his advice, "Do not treat a bad illness so that you become called bad physicians."
And this treatise has been divided into three chapters.
The First Chapter.
On cauterization by fire and cauterization by a sharp medicine, explained in order from the century to the ancient times and images of the instruments and the tools of cauterization and all that is needed for work with the hand.
The Second Chapter.
On incision, excision, venesection, cupping, and surgery, including the extraction of arrows, all explained in order and with images of instruments.
The Third Chapter.
On setting bones, dislocations, and treatment of bone fractures, all explained in order from the century to the ancient times and with images of instruments.
The First Chapter.
On cauterization
And before we describe how to do it, it is necessary to mention the way its benefits and harms are manifest and in what temperament it is used.
And I say that the talk about the manner of the benefit of cauterization and its harms is long speech and a precise science, and a hidden secret, and many of the wise men have spoken about it.
And they disagreed about it, and I have summarized from their words what is brief out of fear of prolixity.
I say that purging is beneficial in general for every bad temperament that is with a substance and without a substance, except for two temperaments: the hot temperament without substance and the dry temperament without substance.
As for the dry temperament with a substance, they have differed about it. Some say that purging is beneficial in it, and others say the opposite, that purging does not benefit in a disease that is from heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
And it is impossible to be cured of a hot and dry disease with a hot and dry medicine, and he who says the opposite says that purging by fire can benefit from a hot and dry disease that occurs in people's bodies. Because when you add to the human body and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you make the human body cold.
And I say what he says because experience has shown me that, except for one who has practiced and studied the art of purging to a great extent. And stood on the difference in temperaments of people and the conditions of diseases in themselves, their causes, symptoms, and duration.
As for the rest of the temperaments, there is no fear from them, especially the cold and wet diseases, since all physicians have agreed on them and have not disagreed about the benefit of purging in them.
And know, my sons, that the secret of treatment is purging by fire and its superiority over purging by burning medicine because fire is a single essence whose action does not exceed the organ that is purged and it does not harm another part connected to it except for slight harm.
And purging by burning medicine may exceed its action to beyond the organs and may cause a disease in an organ that is difficult to treat, or even kill, and fire, because of its nobility and generosity of essence, does not do this except when it is excessive.
It has become clear to us through experience, length of service, attention to the craft, and standing upon the realities of the matter.
For this reason, I have dispensed with lengthy discourse, even though if it were fitting for this book of mine, I would have presented to you in the fire a secret and its manner of action in the bodies and its removal of diseases with philosophical and demonstrative speech that is precise about your understanding.
And know, O sons, that they have differed concerning the time that is suitable for cauterization and made the best time to be the season of spring.
And I say that cauterization is suitable in every time, for the harm caused by the time is dwarfed by the benefit that is obtained through cauterization. Especially if the cauterization is from a necessary and strong pain that is urgent and cannot tolerate delay, for what may follow it in terms of harm might be greater than the slight harm that enters from the time.
And do not think, O sons, what the common people and ignorant physicians imagine that cauterization which cures from a disease never returns to it again and make it an end of the matter.
And it is not appropriate for you to think, because cauterization is like medicine that regulates the constitution and dries up humors which are the cause of pain.
But cauterization is preferred over medicine because of the speed of its success, the strength of its action, and the intensity of its power.
And the disease may return after a time, depending on the constitution of the patient, the strength of his illness, and what is prepared in his body from the gathering of humors within him and neglecting himself in acquiring them from food and suchlike causes.
God willing, except that the disease for which cauterization is used be a mild disease and in an organ with little humors and superfluities. Like the molar tooth and similar pains, it is possible that the pain may not return, and this would be in the least degree.
And as for the saying of the common people that abscess is the last of medicine, this is a correct saying contrary to what they think because they believe that no treatment benefits with medicine or without it after the occurrence of the abscess and the matter is otherwise.
And the meaning of saying that abscess is the last of medicine is that when we used kinds of treatment in a disease and those medicines were ineffective, then we used the last thing, which is the abscess, and it became effective, so from here came the saying that abscess is the last of medicine. Not on the meaning that the common people went to and many ignorant physicians.
And the ancients mentioned that abscess with gold is better than abscess with iron, and they said that because of the moderation of gold and the nobility of its essence, and they said that it does not cause scabbing in the place of the abscess, and this is not at all true.
Because I have tried that and found that it does that in some bodies but not others, and abscess with it is better and more preferable than iron as they said except that if you heat the forceps in the fire from gold it will not be clear to you when it heats to the degree you want for the redness of gold.
And because it quickly cools and if you increase it in heat, it melts in the fire and falls to the craftsman from that in work, so the abscess with iron became faster and more correct for us in work, God willing.
And I have arranged this chapter on abscesses into sections organized from the head to the foot so that it would be easy for the student what he wants from it, God willing.
The first section.
In abscesses of the head there is one kind.
This kind of abscess is beneficial from the excess of moisture and coldness on the brain, which are the cause of headache and increased discharge from the head towards the eyes and ears, and excessive sleep and toothache and throat pain. In summary, for every disease that appears from coldness, like paralysis, epilepsy and stammering and the like.
The image of this method is to order the patient first to purge with a pure laxative medicine for the head three nights or four, according to what is required by the strength of the patient and his age and habit.
Then order him to shave his head with a razor, then make him sit in front of you, seated, with his hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his eyes, and where your middle finger ends, mark that spot with lead.
Then heat the olive iron whose image is this.
If a hole in the skull of the size of the head of a millet or the size of a carnation seed is revealed, raise your hand, otherwise, return your hand with the same iron or another if it cools. Until you see from the bone what I told you, then take some salt and dissolve it in water and soak a cotton ball in it and place it on the spot and leave it for three days.
Then carry a cotton ball soaked in butter on it and leave it until the burning is gone from the fire, then treat him with the four-part ointment until he heals, God willing.
And they said that the wound as long as it remains open expands the pus, which is better and more beneficial.
And some of them mentioned that the skin should be cauterized to the bone and hold the iron until some of the thickness of the bone burns, then after that, what burned from the bone is removed and then treated.
And others said that it is necessary to exaggerate the cauterization until it affects the bone strongly, so that it falls from the bone like the shape of a carbuncle or a small star and they claimed that it releases fumes from the head from that spot and leave the wound open for a long time.
Then he treats it until it heals, and I do not see these two types of wounds except in some people and on the path of rarity. And leaving it with me is better, and safe, if it exists, then the head  grows back when its natural connection is separated as we have seen in the rest of the members.
Especially when the head of the patient is naturally weak, and the first type of wound is safer and better for me, and with it I work so that it heals by God's will.
The Second Chapter.
In the head also.
If in the whole head a chronic pain occurs and has lasted for a long time with the patient, and you have used poultices, cupping, and ointments, and bandages, and especially if he had the single burn we described, and nothing of that helped him, then look. If the patient's head is naturally strong in structure and not weak, and he felt a severe cold, burn another wound slightly above that one. Then burn on each horn of his head a wound until the thickness of the skin goes and exposes the bone to the extent we described. And burn a wound in the back of his head in the place known as the ax, and be light-handed in this one and do not expose the bone because the patient feels a severe pain from it unlike the pain of all other wounds on the head, and I will mention this wound in its place.
And the cautery that burns his horn and back of the head should be gentler than the cautery that burns the middle of the head, and this is its image.
The Third Chapter.
In a chronic headache that has not become worse.
If a pain occurs in the fissure of the head with a headache and the pain extends to the eye, then you should purge the patient with medicinal remedies that purify the head, and use all the treatment I mentioned in the sections on diseases. If it did not help, then cauterize in two ways. Either cauterization with a sharp, hot remedy, or by iron.
As for cauterization with a burning remedy, you take one clove of garlic, peel it and cut off its ends from both sides, then cut the site of pain in the temple with a wide scalpel until it becomes a place under the skin large enough to accommodate the clove.
Then insert it under the skin until it disappears, then pull on it with pliers firmly and tightly, leaving it for about fifteen hours, then remove it and take out the garlic and leave the wound for two or three days, then carry on.
Cover it with cotton soaked in butter until the place is sealed, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. If you wish, do this with some of the burning remedies that I gave you in the eighteenth chapter on burning remedies.
As for cauterization with iron, follow this description: Heat the instrument whose picture is...
And it is called the nail-shaped cautery because its head resembles a nail, with some perforations in it and a small protrusion in its center.
Then place it on the site of pain and hold your hand while you turn the iron slightly, and the amount that burns from the thickness of the skin should be about half of it. And raise your hand so that you do not burn the vein that is below, causing bleeding, then soak cotton in salt water and place it on the site, leaving it for three days. Then carry on with the cotton soaked in butter, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills.
And if you wish, cut this scar with the sharp edge of the cautery and preserve it from cutting the vein in this unchronicled scar, especially.
Chapter Four.
Cauterization of Chronic Scars.
If you treated the headache with what was mentioned of the treatment previously and what was mentioned in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment did not take effect, and you saw from the cause something that does not correspond to what we mentioned of the first type of cauterization by medicine or cauterization by fire. Where you must heat the iron cautery until it whitens after you have learned on the site of the pain in a line equal to half a finger or thereabouts, and leave your hand once while you pull it tight until it cuts the artery and reaches near the bone.
Except that you must be careful not to touch the jaw that moves when chewing, lest it burn the muscle or nerve that moves it and cause a spasm.
And be cautious and careful of bleeding from the artery you cut, for there is danger in cutting it. Especially for one who does not know what to do and has no experience, leaving work first is better.
And the treatment of bleeding from the artery in its place will be mentioned later in the book, if God wills. If you see from the cause something that does not correspond to this cauterization.
And if you see the body of the sick person covered and a cavity like cauterization in the middle of the head, as we described, treat the wound until it heals, if God wills.
And if you wish, use the cauterization mentioned in the chapter on cutting the artery with the two-edged cautery, for it is a better and more effective cauterization than this one.
Chapter Five.
Cauterization of Ear Pains.
If pain occurs in the ear from cold and was treated with laxatives and all the treatments mentioned in the division, and the pain did not go away, then heat the cautery called "the point" which its image is this...
... Then prick with it after heating it around the whole ear, as it revolves or around both of them if the pain is in both ears. And the cauterization is moved away from the origin of the ear a little after you have learned its place with ink, and the cauterization should be about ten dots in each ear or thereabouts, then the places are treated until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Six.
On Cauterizing Tools.
The cauterization tool that is used for treating with the cautery, it is of the type that arises from phlegm as mentioned in the classifications of diseases.
And one should avoid a cauterization tool that arises from the flesh and tightening of the nerve.
When you have treated this type of cauterization tool with the applications and the poultices and the gargles, and your treatment was ineffective, then it is necessary to cauterize the ailment with three cauterizations. One at the origin of the ear, and the second slightly below its ridge, and the third at the junction of the lips.
And make your cauterization from the opposite side of the diseased area because relaxation occurs in the side that appears healthy.
And the shape of the cauterization is to form it with a cauterization facing the upper edge of the ear below the top of the head slightly, and another one in the ridge, and its length should be equal to the length of the thumb.
Lower the cauterization with your hand until it burns about half the thickness of the skin, and this is the shape of the iron which is a type of blade that has advanced in its form but it is slightly gentler than it as you see. And the blade should be slightly thicker, then treat the place with what has been mentioned before until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Seven.
On Cauterizing Chronic Lesions.
If the lesion has been treated and treated with what we have mentioned, and your treatment was ineffective, and there was no fever in the ailment, cauterize it four times. On every part of the head it is so and so in the middle of the head as we have mentioned and so and so in the back of the head as before.
A recipe for cauteries as mentioned previously, and it may also be cauterized so and so on the mouth of the stomach to be more effective, then treated as mentioned before.
The Eighth Chapter.
On forgetfulness.
What arises from phlegm it is necessary to give the sick first drinks of large fruits and brain-purifying seeds.
Then shave his entire head and place on the back of it a poultice of mustard as written in the section on poultices, carry it for several times because it is a type of cautery.
And do it in the exact order that I mentioned there, if he is cured by this otherwise make three cauterizations on the back of his head placed one above the other from the top of the head to below the neck.
And make between each cauterization and cauterization the thickness of a finger, then treat the cauterization as mentioned before, if you want to increase it and the sick person is capable of it make a cauterization in the middle.
If you want to increase it then cauterize on the two horns, and treat it until he is cured, and the cautery would be olive oil in the form mentioned before.
The Ninth Chapter.
On cauterization for paralysis and relaxation of the whole body.
It is necessary that you proceed in purifying the head with fruits and what we have mentioned, then shave the head of the sick person and cauterize one cautery in the middle of the head, one on each horn of the head, and one on its back.
And three on the vertebrae of the neck, if you need in a case of relaxation of the body to more than that and the patient is capable of it, and the illness is strong and stubborn make four cauterizations on the vertebrae of his back. Apply heat to the cauterization until most of it is burned from the skin and then raise your hand, and then treat it according to what has been mentioned before until it heals, God willing, and the cautery tool should be olive oil-based.
Chapter Ten.
On Epilepsy.
Only the epileptic who has epilepsy due to phlegm should be cauterized, and it is necessary that his nose be cleansed first with large syringes and with all the treatments mentioned in the section if the patient is large and likely to take medicine.
As for if he is a child who cannot tolerate medicine, let him use gargles and mouthwashes that cleanse the brain before that for many days with improvement of his nutrition.
Then he shaves his head and then cauterizes one cautery in the middle of the head as mentioned before, and another cautery in the back of his head. And on each horn of his head, a cautery; if the patient is strong and likely, cauterize with the cauteries mentioned in the chapter on paralysis, and relax the body on the vertebrae of the neck and vertebrae of the back, and the cautery tool should be olive oil-based according to the description that has come before.
If the patient is a child, make the cautery gentle on this picture.
Chapter Eleven.
On Cauterizing Mania.
If the cause of mania is rotten humors and thick phlegm, cauterize with the cauteries mentioned in the chapter on paralysis.
If the cause of mania is an excess that tends towards black and the body of the patient is damp and rotten, cleanse his nose as mentioned before in the section.
Then shave the head of the patient and then make a tight cake of cotton like a circle and put it in the middle of his head and the patient is sitting upright holding onto each side, then take one handful of old sheep fat.
Then he heats it on the fire with moderate heat as much as the finger can bear when inserted in it, then empty its center at the top of its head in a circle and leave it until it cools, do this to the patient every week once with his other good treatment until he heals, God willing.
And if you wish, you can heat it with small points without holding your hand to the hot iron, and this type of heating moistens the brain moderately.
Then put cotton soaked in ghee or chicken fat on it.
The Twelfth Chapter.
Regarding the treatment of water flowing into the eye.
If you notice the beginning of water flowing into the eye with the signs mentioned in the division, hasten to treat the patient by drying his head and protecting him from all dampness and sweat him in a bath on an empty stomach for days.
Then, once more shave his head and apply a hot iron in the middle of the head and then apply two hot irons on the temples if the water is flowing from both eyes or from one side if it is from one eye.
Then, cut all the veins and arteries under the skin with a hot iron. Let the irons be long in width across the temples and protect from bleeding.
If you see anything of it, cut it on the spot with any treatment that is possible and I will come to you with wisdom in cauterizing the arteries and cutting them and protecting from bleeding.
And sometimes two strong hot irons can be applied on the back of the head under the bones.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
Regarding the treatment of chronic tears.
If the tears of the eye are chronic and constant and were from the veins and arteries on the surface of the head outside the head, and you are certain that this is due to a cold and thick phlegm in the body, then apply the hot iron cauterization described earlier for the treatment of water flowing into the eye. A cautery in the middle of the head and two cauteries on the temples and two cauteries in the nape of the neck under the bones, and if it needs an increase then put a cautery on each side of the temple at the edge of the eyebrow with a small iron.
Chapter fourteen.
On cauterizing the nose.
If you treated him with what was mentioned in the division and the treatment did not work, then hasten to cauterize the patient three nights, then shave his head and cauterize the middle part with a greenish iron. Then cauterize with the nail-shaped iron two cauteries above the eyebrows under the hair a little, and beware of the artery, do not cut it, and this is the image of the nail-shaped iron.
Chapter fifteen.
On cauterizing the eyelid.
If the eyelid relaxes due to a disease or dampness, cauterize the eyelid with one cautery using this crescent-shaped iron.
And if you wish, cauterize above the eyebrows slightly two cauteries on each side and keep it away from the temples, and let the length of each cautery be equal to the length of the eyebrow.
And do not overdo your hand with the cauterization, but only as much as one-third of the skin burns, and the image of the iron is like this.
Chapter sixteen.
On cauterizing the eyelid.
If its lashes turned inward and caused pain in the eye, then there are two types of cautery for it. Either cauterization with fire or cauterization with a burning medicine, as for cauterization with fire, you order the patient before that to leave his lashes if he is one of those who trims them until they grow long and even.
If it is cauterized while growing, then tighten his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until it grows, and if it has grown and become even, put the patient's head in your lap and learn on the eyelid with lead as a mark resembling the shape of a lotus leaf.
The beginning of the sign should be near the eyelids, then under the eyelid cotton soaked in egg white or in the saliva of the squill is placed, and a hot iron is applied to it, its shape as follows.
Then it is cauterized in the shape which was taught, little by little, many times until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a whole myrtle leaf, appears distinctly and particularly; a sign of the healthiness of your work is seeing that the eyelid becomes charred and the hair rises from the edge of the eye.
Raise your hand then and leave it for three days, then apply cotton smeared with butter until the scab falls off, then treat it with ointment until it heals, God willing. If something of the hair returns after some time and the eyelid relaxes.
Then repeat the cauterization on that spot as you did at first, if the hair is in the lower eyelid, burn it until it returns to its natural place and does not fall out; as for cauterizing with a burning medicine, tell the sick person to leave his eyelids until they grow long and become equal.
Then you make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf, and take from the usual soap and un-slaked lime, one dram each, or thereabouts; pound them both well together, and do this quickly so that they do not dry. Then spread it on the parchment which you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it on one or both eyelids, and put cotton soaked in egg white under the eye, and the head of the sick person in a stone (or block).
And you put your index finger above the medicine and press it slightly, and move it whenever the sick person feels the sting of the medicine because he will feel it like fire; as long as he feels the stinging, leave the medicine and move it with your finger; if the stinging stops, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
Look, if you see the eyelid raised as it is when one winces at fire or a cut, otherwise apply medicine to the place that was not affected by it and did not turn black until you finish your work and the eye winces, then put cotton soaked in fat on it until the stinging of the burn subsides.
Then treat it with a balm of palm or otherwise until it heals, and it is necessary for you when working to be extremely careful that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye. If the eyelid relaxes after days and we fear something from the hair enters the eye.
Then apply the medicine to that place where the eyelid relaxed, especially as you did at first, then treat it until it heals, and this is a picture of a leaf of the ash tree.
Know that people's eyes differ in size, so accordingly let your wincing be, and it is not hidden the right way for one who has experience in this craft.
The seventeenth chapter.
Concerning a pimple that appears on the white of the eye.
If you treated the pimple with what we mentioned in the classifications of diseases and your treatment did not work, then it is necessary to cauterize it in this manner.
Order the patient to place his head in a block and have a servant hold his head between your hands, holding it so that it does not move or strike against anything.
Then place cotton soaked in egg white or the saliva of the bergamot plant on his eyes, then heat the cauterizing iron whose image is shown here.
It should be hollow like a tube of an eagle's feather from one end which will be used for cauterizing, and if you want it to have an opening at the other end, or if you want it to be solid like a ramrod, except that this hollow one is better for your work, God willing.
Then, you squeeze the abscess if it is open and the pus comes out, and you dry it. Or if it is not open, you open it and extract its pus, then you place the plate on it, which is very protective, so hold it with your hand until it reaches the bone.
And pull your hand a little away at the swelling from the eye towards the direction of the nose so that your hand does not make a mistake or the patient moves and the plate falls into the eyelid and spoils it. If it reached the bone at the first attempt, otherwise, return the plate again for another time if you need to do so.
And leave him for three days, then apply cotton wool with butter on it and treat it with the drying ointment until it heals. If forty days have passed and it has not healed, then apply the strong medication to make the bone appear and separate it as will be mentioned in its chapter if God wills.
And another way for treating an abscess which some of the ancients mentioned, is to go to the place of the abscess, cut it open and put a thin funnel in the same incision, this is its image.
And pour into it a weight of a dirham of molten lead, and hold your hand on the funnel firmly, so that it does not move at all and the patient does not move even a bit so that the molten lead doesn't flow into his eye, and it is necessary to place cotton wool over the patient's eye, soaked in egg white or water.
For the lead burns the place of the abscess and heals it with a miraculous healing, if the abscess heals by what we have mentioned of cutting and treatment, otherwise, there is no escape from using the nasal passage and returning the abscess to its path in the nose as will be mentioned in its specific chapter.
The Eighteenth Chapter.
In Treating a Cleft Lip.
A cleft lip often happens, called a "harelip," especially in the lips of boys, as it happens frequently. If this cleft lip is treated with what we have mentioned in the division and the treatment didn't work, then you take a small, dagger-like plate like this image.
Make its cavity on the sharpness of the knife, then place it guardedly in the same fissure until the point reaches the depth of the fissure, then treat it with the quirit until it heals, God willing.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
On a wound of the mouth, caused by a knife.
If it appears in the root of the gums or on the palate or in the roots of the teeth, a swelling then bursts and becomes an abscess, then you treat it but the treatment is ineffective, then it is necessary to place a heated iron over it as much as the abscess allows.
Then insert it guardedly into the hole of the abscess and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depths, both ends, and do this once or twice, then treat it afterward with what we have mentioned from treatment until it heals, God willing.
If the material stops and heals, otherwise, it is necessary to open the place and remove the rotten bone according to what will come in its chapter, God willing.
The Twentieth Chapter.
On a wound of the teeth and gums, which are relaxed.
If the gums have relaxed due to moisture and the teeth have moved, and you have treated it with medicines but they were ineffective, place the head of the patient in your stone, then heat the iron whose image comes after this after placing the tube on the tooth.
And insert the iron guardedly with haste, and hold your hand a little until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth, then raise your hand, then repeat the iron several times as you desire, then have the patient fill their mouth with salt water.
And he holds it for an hour and spits it out, for the moved tooth will become fixed, and the relaxed gums will tighten, and the putrid moisture will dry up.
Chapter Twenty-One.
On the pain of the tooth.
If the pain of the tooth is from cold or there is a worm in it and there is no relief from treatment with medicines, then the cure for it is in two ways: either by cauterization with fat or by cauterization with fire.
As for cauterization with fat, take the cow butter and melt it in an iron spoon or a pan, then take cotton wool and wrap it on the tip of the probe, then dip it in the melted butter and put it on the aching tooth quickly and hold it until it cools.
Then repeat it several times until the strength of the fire reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, dip a cotton swab or wool in cold butter and put it on the aching tooth and place a heated iron above it until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth.
As for cauterization with fire, proceed to a copper or iron tube with some thickness in its body so that the heat of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient, then heat the soldering iron which comes with its image and place it on the same tooth and hold your hand until the soldering iron cools. Do this several times.
Then the pain goes either on that same day or the next day, and it is necessary after that cauterization to fill the mouth of the patient with good butter and hold it for an hour then spit it out, and this is the image of the soldering iron.
It can be cauterized with any side you want and at the calculation that is possible, and this is the image of the tube.
Chapter Twenty-Two.
On the cauterization of swine.
If the swine are from phlegm and cold humidity and they do not respond to maturation with medicines, and you want a quick maturation, then heat the hollow soldering iron whose image is shown here with both ends penetrating.
To cause the smoke to exit from the cauterizing instrument at its other end, place it over the tumor itself once and again if necessary until you reach the depth of the tumor. And if the tumor is small, make the cautery commensurate with the size of the tumor.
Then leave it for three days and apply upon it cotton soaked in ghee until what was burned by the fire goes away, then treat it with ointment and fumigations until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Twenty-Third.

Then treat him with what was mentioned before until he heals, God willing.
Chapter Twenty-Fourth.
In cauterization, a lung disease and cough are cured.

The Twenty-Fifth Chapter.

The Twenty-Sixth Chapter.
In a Cauterization of the Abdomen.

The Twenty-Eighth Chapter.
Cauterizing a Liver Tumor.
If a tumor appears in the liver and you want to know whether it is in the liver flesh or its peritoneum, if it is in the liver flesh, the patient will find heaviness and pain without sharpness.
And if it is in the peritoneum of the liver, there will be pain with extreme sharpness and you saw that physicians have been unable to treat it, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on his back and then learn the location of the tumor with lead pencil.
Then heat the cauterizer in the fire, it is the cauterizer that resembles a mill, and this is its image. And cauterize it with one cauterization until you burn all the skin and end the cauterization to reach the peritoneum until the lead pencil comes out, then treat it with the treatment of abscesses until it heals.
And this type of cauterization should not be used except by one whose path in medicine has been long and who has practiced these diseases repeatedly, so then he proceeds with such work and leaving it to me is better.
The Twenty-Ninth Chapter.

Then it is shaped as one mass between the attachment of the collarbone and the neck, and two small masses a little below the armpits, slightly inclined towards the side under the chin, and two large masses above the breasts, between the third and fourth ribs.
And two masses also between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly inclined to the back, and one mass in the middle of the chest and another above the stomach, and three masses from behind, one between the shoulder blades and two on either side of the spine below the mass that is between the palms.
And it is not necessary for your hand to go deep into the mass, but it should be a feeling under the skin, and some of the ancients mentioned that there are people who use an iron hotplate similar to a trowel, heat it, and insert it between the ribs until it reaches the tumor itself.
And it is removed as we mentioned in the case of a liver tumor, and in this case, puncturing the mass with pus, either the patient may die from the hour of its removal, or there may appear in the place a sore that does not heal.

Chapter Forty-One.
In case of sciatica.

So that the circle encircles the entire hip and burns the thickness of all the skin, this is the characteristic of the splint in sciatica if the pain is persistent to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.

And be careful in all your cauterizations that the cautery does not reach to burn a nerve or a large artery so that it causes harm to the patient, either a bad consequence or a long time illness.
And I have seen one and another who was cauterized above the ankle and pus came from the cautery, the leg swelled until it reached the foot and all of it became infected and rotten, then diarrhea occurred and death followed after that. If the pain is in both sides, cauterize them both in this same manner.
And some of the wise scholars have mentioned in cauterizing the hip, that it should be made like a goblet from iron and its diameter is half a cubit and at its mouth it should be as thick as the kernel of a date or slightly less, and inside that goblet there is another goblet and a third goblet.
And what is between each goblet should be the size of a thumb knuckle and the goblets are open from both sides, and their height is about one or two knuckles. They take handles made of iron which are firmly held in the goblets, and this is its form.
Then it is heated in the fire until it becomes red hot and sparks fly, then it is placed on the right hip of the patient leaning on the healthy side, cauterizing three circular lines at once, then leave him for three days, and bandage him with butter, and leave the wound open for days.
Many ulcers are treated with ointment until they heal, said the compiler of this book, this type of ulcer is rarely used because of its ugliness and bad appearance, and few people can endure it except that for those who endure it well it is a good kind of ulcer to have if it happens in the right place.
As for ulcers treated with cauterizing medications, it is made to create two basins shaped like the throat into which a red-hot spatula of copper or iron descends.
They have a rim around the edge, about two fingers high or so, and after them there is a space between them equal to the thickness of a finger, they are open at the bottom and open at the top, and some of them are clasped together like this.
Then they are lowered onto the back of the hip and the ulcer, the patient lying on his healthy side, you hold their hand firmly, then pour between the two basins hot water, heated by a brazier, and hold it for an hour's time, and the patient endures its burning, as he feels a burning sensation like fire.
Until the burning sensation subsides, then you raise your hand with the tool and wipe away the hot water from the entire hip with fresh water, and leave him for three days, and apply butter to it until the blackness of the burn disappears, and leave it for days until pus drains from it, as it is more beneficial.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals, and if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, a basin is made for him similar to that used on the hip, this is the description of hot water, which I have established in the treatise on correcting medications.
Take from the salt of the kidney and slaked lime, one part of each, grind them together and put them in a new pot with a single small hole at the bottom, just big enough for the red-hot spatula to fit through, and place another pot filled with water under it.
Pour on the kidney and litharge an amount of fresh water that covers them with your finger after you have squeezed them well in your hand, then leave the pot until the sharp water goes down to the bottom of the pot. Then gather all that water and pour it on another litharge and another kidney, renewing them also.
For then it becomes at that time very powerful in sharpness, and acts in many works of medicine and for all the other members because it does the action of fire itself, and there are some medicines that are heated with it also like the Thafssia, honey of the blader, litharge with soap being ground.
And Galen claimed a story about an ancient man's treatment for hip pain and sciatica, extolling its importance greatly, claiming that it does not need anything else from treatments, and that it cures in one time.
Until that he may have entered the bath being carried and come out of it cured, which is to take from the green shitirj, if it is not found green, then take the fresh one, grind it well with something of fat and place it on the hip where the pain is or in the leg or thigh.
And tighten it and leave it for three hours or as long as the patient feels a cessation of burning, then put him in the bath, and if his body is relaxed, put him in the basin because the pain goes away and he is cured by God's permission, but if he does not get cured, repeat the poultice after ten days once more.
For it cures if God wills, and know that it is not appropriate for anyone to use this medicine except after emptying the body, and Dioscorides mentioned that goat's urine when heated with sciatica benefited from it.
And the litharge is like this, take wool and soak it in old oil and place it on the deep place between the thumb of the hand and the ulna, which is closer to the ulna, then take dry goat's urine.
Then ignite it with fire until it becomes embers, then place it on wool and leave it until it goes out, then take another one and continue doing so until the sensation reaches from the middle of the arm to the hip, and the pain subsides by God's will. This type of beating is called cupping.
Chapter Forty-two.
Cupping for Back Pain.
Back pain may arise from many causes, either from a fall or a blow or excessive vomiting, and the like.  It is caused by a cold, wet substance being deposited there, and cupping is applied to this type alone.
That which is caused by a cold substance, after vomiting the patient should be cupped on his back where the pain is, three rows across the same width as the table. After marking the place with lead in each row, five cups or more should be applied according to what you see of the patient's ability and strength.
The cupping should be done with a single point cautery, and if you wish, three or four cups can be applied with a medium-sized nail cautery in this manner.
Chapter Forty-three.
Cupping for the Beginning of the Hump.
This ailment often afflicts young children, and the sign of its beginning in a child is shortness of breath when standing up and moving, and you will find at the end of his spine vertebrae protruding more than the rest.
If you see this and want to stop it, cup with a circular cautery in this manner. To take the cupping on each side of the vertebra equally, and if you wish, cup around the vertebra with a single point cautery in two or three rows, and let the points be close to each other, then treat the area until it heals as we have mentioned.
And beware that you use cautery in the swelling which results from the stretching of the nerve.
Chapter Forty-Fourth.
On cauterizing gout and joint pain.
If the joint pain is due to cold moisture that settles in any part of the body, and if it occurs in the legs, it is customary for physicians to call it gout in particular.
And if the cold gout is treated with the remedies mentioned in the classification and the pain does not go away, then cautery removes it, which is to make after emptying around the joint of the leg many cauteries, and they are olive-colored medium on this form.
And if it is necessary to cauterize on the leg, do so with a pointed cautery. If the pain ascends to the knees or to other joints, and this happens often, then you should cauterize each knee three or four times from each side with that same olive-colored cautery.
And if it is necessary to do more than this cauterization, cauterize, but do not deepen your hand in the cautery, but it should be about the thickness of the skin only. If the pain ascends to the hips or back, use what was mentioned from the cautery in its chapter.
And if the pain is in the hands only, cauterize around the wrists as two circles. If the pain remains in the fingers, cauterize each knuckle and on the palm of the hand. If the pain ascends after days to the elbows or armpits.
Then cauterize them from each side, and let the patient not be without good care and taking medication, for if he has good food and empties phlegm, he will be cured with this cautery, God willing.
Chapter Forty-Fifth.
On Treating Ligatures
If a hernia appears in the groin and some of the intestine and the omentum have descended into the testicle and this is starting recently, it becomes necessary to order the patient to refrain from eating for a day and to use emollient remedies that bring down the bowels from his abdomen.
Then, he should lie down on his back in front of you and you should order him to hold himself until the omentum or intestine protrudes and then push it back with your finger, then learn by the pencil under the hernia on the bone of the pubic arch a mark resembling half a circle, its edges towards the upper body.
Then you apply heat to this form.
Until it becomes white and throws sparks, then you push the intestine or omentum back into his abdomen, then a servant puts his hand on the place so that the intestine does not protrude and someone else has placed a cushion under him and another servant ties on his legs.
And another one on his chest holding his hands, then you put the iron on the same mark and your hand with the iron standing straight and hold it until it reaches the bone or repeat it again if it doesn't reach in the first time to the bone.
And be careful of your effort from the protrusion of the intestine while you cauterize it so that you do not burn it and this causes great harm to the patient, either death or a terrible injury. Know that when you don't reach the bone with the cauterization, your work has not been successful, and it is necessary for the iron of the boys to be gentle on their bodies and for the adults on theirs.
Then you treat the place of cauterization after three days with butter until the dryness of the fire disappears, then treat it with all ointments until it heals. Let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
It is necessary to make his food during his treatment as follows: he should lie down on his stomach so that the intestine does not protrude when he moves or sits, then if he wants to get up after forty days, you use a tight bandage and hold it for another forty days and reduce fatigue and fullness from food and drink and loud shouting.
If he employs this method thus, may Allah grant him complete healing by his will, and I will mention the treatment of hernia by incision in its own chapter, if He wills.  But as for the hernia that occurs in the rest of the abdomen and is at its beginning, if you wish it not to increase, fill the hernia with a round quantity that corresponds to its size. Let what is burned from the skin be like one-third of it, and then treat it with what has been mentioned, for it will not increase if Allah wills. And some of the ancients have mentioned that the hernia should be cauterized with a triangular iron like this image.
After you have learned to draw the hernia with the pencil and make a line on its upper side in the lateral direction, and the other line downward, and then put your hand in the middle with a single, nail-like quantity, and the first cauterization is easier and better if Allah wills.
The Sixth Forty Chapter.
