Chapter twenty-four.
On treating the growing flesh in the nose.
Sometimes growths in the nose may appear as various kinds of flesh, some resembling scorpions with many legs, and others like cancerous, hardened flesh the color of lead, and others soft flesh that is not the color of lead.
As for any of these growths that are soft and not cancerous or malignant, it is necessary to have the patient sit before you facing the sun, open his nostrils, and insert a probe into those growths, then draw them outward, then cut what you have grasped with a sharp and fine scalpel from one side.
Until you know that all the flesh has gone, and if anything remains that you could not cut, remove it with one of the fine instruments gently until nothing remains. If blood overcomes you or a hot swelling appears.
Then treat it with what is appropriate, and if it was from malignant tumors, act quickly to cut them until the blood stops and all the flesh goes away, then after cutting, put into the nose clear water or a drink, so that the nose opens and moisture flows from it into the throat.
Know that it is cured, and if the moisture does not flow as it should, know that inside, flesh has grown in the upper part of the loose bone, which the instrument did not reach with the cutting, so then it is necessary to take a cotton thread of some thickness.
And tie many knots in it and make between each knot the size of a finger or less, so that the patient can insert one end of the thread into his nose with force or as much as he can after making it like beads, and draw air through it until it reaches the nostrils.
And it comes out on his throat, and often children do this in school, which is easy for anyone who wants to do it, then gather the two ends of the thread, one that came out on the mouth and the other that remained in the nose.
Then you apply the spreading of the flesh with a thread tied to it, doing this until you learn that the flesh has been cut by the thread, then you remove the thread and place it in the nose after wiping the blood, using a wick soaked in Egyptian ointment, doing this for three days or more.
Until the ointment consumes all that remains of the flesh, and what is left in the nose becomes a lead pipe for days until it heals. If it needs treatment to dry up, use this.
This is an image of the instrument used to drip ointments and medicines into the nose:.
It has silver or brass, shaped like a small wick holder, open at the tip with its channel as well.
And if you wish, you can make the tube closed like a pipe and the ointment container flat.
It has a handle at its end as you see, held when it is heated with the fat or whatever you wish of juices or flowing things.
The Twenty-Fifth Chapter.
Regarding warts that sprout at the tip of the nose.
Many times, a wart grows at the tip of the nose and becomes larger and multiplies with the days until it is unsightly to look at.
Therefore, it should be cut at its first appearance and all of it should be removed, then apply to the area either cauterization or a burning medicine that replaces cauterization. If it is missed being cut until it becomes large, look, if it is hard and solid like wood and has little sensation.
Do not expose it to iron, for it is a cancerous tumor and I have often seen that when this tumor is cut, it returns with great harm to its owner. If the tumor is soft to the touch and not like wood, and you see that it can be cut completely. Then evacuate the tumor and cut it without hesitation or worry, and treat the area with what dries it up and constricts it until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-six
On the Sewing of the Nose and Lip and Ear. If the attachment of it becomes separated from a wound or the like, know that when separation of the attachment occurs in one of these cartilages, little that is useful is done in most cases.
When it is presented to you that one of these things has occurred, examine whether the wound is fresh with blood; if so, bring together the edges of the wound with sutures and then treat it until it heals. And if the separation of the attachment has spread its edges and each incision has become firm, then it is necessary to excise each incision with the thickness of its outer skin until it bleeds.
Then bring together the edges with sutures, tighten them, and place upon them a dressing of mastic and frankincense powder; and place above the dressings a poultice of palm wax ointment or another adhering ointment, and leave it fastened for two or three days, then remove it.
And change the dressing, and leave it until the threads detach themselves, then treat it with ointment until it heals. And the description of the sutures is to bring together the separation of the attachment either with needles as we described in sewing the abdomen, or with thread as we explained there.
Chapter Twenty-seven
On the Removal of Nodes that Appear on the Lips.
Many people may have small, hard tumors inside their lips, some resembling a wart and others smaller and larger. It is necessary to turn the lip and make an incision on each node and stitch it with the forceps.
And cut it from each side, then fill the place after cutting with powdered za'atar until the bleeding stops, and rinse it with vinegar and salt; treat the places, as much as possible, with a bandage until the wounds heal.
The Eighteenth Chapter
In cutting away excess flesh in the gums.
Often excess flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call abulus. It is necessary to tie it with a thread or hold it with a forceps and cut it at its root and leave the discharge of fluid or blood then place on the site powdered zinc.
Or one of the gripping, drying cones; if that flesh returns after treatment, it often returns so cut it again and cauterize it; for it does not return after cauterization.
The Twenty-Ninth Chapter
In filing teeth with iron.
There may gather on the surfaces of the teeth, from inside and outside and between the gums, rough, unsightly scales; they may turn dark and yellow and green until a putrid condition reaches the gums and disfigures the teeth because of it.
Then it is necessary to have the patient sit before you and his head in a block, and file the molars and teeth which appear to you with scales and something like sand until nothing remains of them; and do likewise for the blackness, the greenness, the yellowing, and the like until they are purified.
If what is in it goes with the first filing, otherwise, file it again on another day and then a third until you reach the end of what you desire; know that the molar requires different shapes and many forms of files according to what suits your work.
For the file that files the molar from inside is not the file that files it from outside, and the one that files between the molars is of another form; and these are several forms of files that you have all prepared:
The Thirtieth Chapter
In extracting teeth.
It is necessary to treat the molar for its pain with every means and delay its extraction; there is no replacement if it is extracted because it is a noble essence, even if there is no other choice but to extract it.
It is necessary that if the sick person intends to have his tooth extracted, he be stabilized until the aching tooth becomes well for you. For often the sick person is deceived by the pain and thinks that it is in the healthy tooth, so he extracts it, then the pain does not go away until the diseased tooth is extracted; we have seen this from the actions of barbers many times.
If the aching tooth becomes well for you, then it is necessary that you encircle the tooth with a scalpel that has some strength so that the gums are separated from all sides, and then move it with your fingers or gently by means of instruments first little by little until you loosen it.
Then you will be able to grasp it with the large pliers firmly and the head of the sick person between your knees, so that he does not move, then pull the tooth in a straight line lest you break it; if it does not come out except  then take one of those instruments and insert it under it from all sides gently and move it as you did before.
And if the tooth is perforated or decayed, it is necessary that you fill that hole with lint and plug it firmly with a fine tip of a reed so that it does not come loose while you pull on it with pliers; and it is necessary that you investigate around the gums from all sides well.
And be cautious of your effort so that you do not break it, so that some of it remains and returns to the sick person from harm greater than his first pain; and beware of doing what ignorant barbers do in their haste and taking out a tooth without using what we have described.
For often they cause great harm to people, the least of which is that the tooth breaks and its roots or some of them remain. Or perhaps he extracts with some of the jawbone as we have seen many times; then, after extracting it, rinse with a drink or vinegar and salt; if blood occurs from the place, then often this happens, so crush some alum and pack the place with it.
But if the saffron does not benefit you, picture the long handles and short knobs of forceps that are used to move a tooth.  They should be thick so they do not bend when you grasp them on the tooth, and this is a picture of large forceps:
They should be thick in the handles so that when you grasp them they do not give way or bend, and short in the arms. They should be made of Indian iron or well-tempered steel, with pointed tips that fit together tightly so that they grip firmly.
And their ends may be shaped like the handle of a chisel, and also strong in their hold.
Chapter Thirty-Third.
On Extracting Tooth Roots and Removing Broken Jawbones.
If a root remains after extracting a tooth and it has broken, you should place cotton soaked in butter on the spot for one or two days until the area relaxes, then insert forceps or tweezers. Which resemble the beak of a bird called the bulbul, and this is a picture of the forceps:
They should be made like a chisel from the inside or like an awl. If these forceps do not help in removing it, you should excavate around the root and expose all of the flesh with a knife, then insert a tool that resembles a small drill, whose picture is:
Short in the tip, slightly thick, and not pointed so that it does not break. If the root comes out with this, otherwise, rely on these other tools whose picture is: The first one is triangular at its tip with some thickness:
A picture of another fine triangle:
And we can also rely on this tool with two prongs, whose picture is also:
And with other tools and chisels mentioned earlier in the chapter on teeth, we can also rely on this tool that resembles a large awl, whose picture is:
The tip of the bent instrument is somewhat thickened so that it does not break, and it is not straight. Know that there are many instruments for teeth, as well as all other instruments, which can hardly be counted. The skilled craftsman in his craft may invent tools for himself according to what work and diseases themselves indicate.
Because some diseases have not been mentioned for which the ancients made instruments due to the difference in their types, if a bone of the jaw or one of the bones of the mouth breaks or decays, then search for it in its place with what is suitable for it from among these instruments and the probes mentioned in extracting the roots.
And we assist ourselves by the figure of this image:.
It should be somewhat thickened to hold the bone so that it does not slip until the bone is extracted, and we force the place with appropriate medicines. If the bone has slight decay, remove its decay and blackness until it is purified, then treat it until it heals.
The Second Thirty Chapter.
In the Planting of Teeth that Have Sprouted on Others.
If the molars sprout in a place other than their natural course, they become unsightly, especially if this happens to women and slaves. It is necessary to examine whether the molar has sprouted behind another molar.
And if its sprouting or returning was not possible, then remove it. If it is stuck to another molar, cut it off with this instrument, whose image is:
It resembles a small beak, and let it be made of very sharp Indian steel, and make your cuts to it over many days because of the hardness of the molar so that it does not shake any other molars. But if it is rooted firmly, then pull it out with a file from India whose image is:
It should be all from India, and its tip is very finely engraved. It should be like the file used to make needles. With it, pull out the molar little by little over many days gently so that the tooth does not shake and fall, then finish smoothing it and remove it with some pliers.
If a tooth has broken off from it and it causes pain to the tongue when speaking, it is necessary to cool it also until the harshness of that fracture disappears and it becomes level and smooth so that the tongue is not hurt nor is speech impaired.
The Third Thirty-Third Chapter.
On Wiring Teeth with Silver or Gold Thread.
If the front teeth are loosened and moved by a blow or fall, and the patient cannot bite on anything to eat lest they fall out, and they were treated with astringent medicines but the treatment was not effective in them.
The solution in this case is to tie them with a thread of gold or silver, and gold is better because silver rusts and decays after some days, while gold remains as it is forever without any change; and the thread should be of medium thickness and appropriate for the space between the teeth.
And the image of wiring is that you take the thread and insert its loop between the two healthy teeth, then weave the ends of the thread between the loosened teeth, one or more, until the weaving reaches the healthy tooth from the other side.
Then, you return the weaving to where it began and tighten your hand with care and wisdom so that they do not move at all; and your tightening of the thread should be at the roots of the teeth so that it does not come loose. Then, you cut off the excess ends of the thread with scissors, gather them together, and tie them with a thread and hide them between the healthy tooth and the loosened tooth.
So that it does not hurt the tongue, then you leave it like this tied for as long as needed. If it breaks or is cut, re-tie it with another thread; and he enjoys it in this way his whole life. This is an image of the teeth and the appearance of wiring in two healthy teeth and two loosened teeth, as you see:
A single tooth or two may return to their place after falling out and interlock as we described, and remain. But this is done by a maker of a path who is a companion, and he may carve bone from the bones of an ox and make it in the form of a tooth and place it in the place where the tooth went. And he tightens it as we said, and it remains, and he enjoys that.
Chapter Forty-Third.
In cutting the ligament which appears under the tongue and prevents speech.
This ligament that appears under the tongue may be either natural, born with it by a human, or it may be acquired from an injury that has healed.
And the work in it is to open the mouth of the patient and his head in a brick and raise his tongue, then cut that nervous ligament across until the tongue releases from its hold. If there is some stiffness and complexity in it and it was from a healed wound, make a splint for it and cut it across until the ligament breaks apart and the knot unravels.
And beware that the cut be in the depth of the flesh so that a vein is cut there and bleeding occurs. Then, rinse after the cut with rose water or vinegar and cold water, then put under the tongue a wick of cotton which the patient grasps every night.
Lest it stick together again, if bleeding occurs, place on the spot powdered turmeric, and if the blood overcomes you, cauterize the place with a lens-shaped soldering iron suitable for this purpose. Then treat him with all treatment until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-Third.
In removing the tadpole that is born under the tongue.
A tumor may occur under the tongue resembling a small tadpole which prevents the tongue from doing its natural function, and perhaps it hardens until it fills the mouth. And the work in it is to open the patient's mouth facing the sun and look at the tumor.
If you see it as a dark color or black, firm and the sick person feels no sensation in it, do not touch it, for it is cancer. But if it is inclined to whiteness and there is moisture in it, then insert the forceps into it and cut it with a fine scalpel and remove it from every direction.
If blood overcomes you while working, put powdered alum on it until the bleeding stops, then return to your work until you remove it completely, and then gargle with vinegar and salt.
Then treat him with all the appropriate treatment until he heals.
Chapter Thirty-Six.
On the Treatment of Tonsil Tumors.
And what grows in the throat from other tumors, which may appear inside the throat, glands resembling those that appear externally and are called tonsils, if treated with what was mentioned in the classification but did not heal.
Look, if the tumor is firm, dark in color, and has little sensation, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red in color and its base is thick, do not touch it either with iron for fear of bleeding, but leave it until it matures, either that you will press it down or that it bursts from itself.
And if it is white in color, round and its base is soft, this is what should be cut. And the work to be done is that you look before working, if it has settled with its heat a complete stillness or some deficiency of deficiency.
Then, when this happens, have the patient sit facing the sun and his head in a block. You open his mouth and take an assistant beside you, who presses his tongue down with a tool whose image is:
It is made of silver or copper and is thin like a knife. If you press it with it, the tongue will be pressed down, and the tumor and its location will become clear to you. Then take forceps and insert them into the tonsil and pull them outwards as much as possible without pulling anything from the peritoneum along with them.
Then it is cut with an instrument whose shape resembles shears, only the ends of each are bent so that the edge of one meets the edge of the other very sharply. It is made of Indian steel or Damascus steel.
If this instrument is not available, then cut it with a scalpel whose image is:
Sharp on one side and blunt on the other. After cutting one almond, cut the other in the same manner, then after cutting, gargle the patient's throat with cold water or vinegar and water.
If he experiences bleeding, gargle with water in which the rind of pomegranates or myrtle leaves or something similar has been steeped until the bleeding stops, then treat him until it heals.  And tumors may grow in the throat other than the tonsils, so they are cut as described for cutting the tonsils.
And I treated a woman who had a tumor that had grown inside her throat, pressing on the esophagus, barely leaving space for breathing and she was barely able to eat or drink.
And she was close to death if she had stayed for a day or two, and the tumor protruded from it with two branches until they came out through her nostrils. I acted quickly and inserted a hook into one of them and pulled it, and a piece that was suitable was pulled out.
Then I cut it where I reached it from the nostrils, and then I did the same with what protruded from the other nostril, then I opened her mouth and pressed down on her tongue, and inserted the hook into the tumor itself, and cut some of it out. And only a little blood came out.
Then the woman's throat opened up, and she immediately started drinking water, then she ate food, and we continued to cut from that tumor repeatedly for a long time, and the tumor would replace what was cut until it took me and her a long time.
I incised and removed the tumor within the throat, so it ceased to increase and then I traveled from there and I do not know what God did with it after that.
The seventh thirty chapter.
On cutting a tumor of the palate.
The one that is called a grape if it descended downward into the palate and swelled, and was white and oblong; then it is called a column, and if it is thick at the bottom and round, then it is called a grape. If it was treated with what has been mentioned in the classification, and the treatment was not effective.
And I saw the hot tumor had subsided from it, and it was tender; it is necessary to cut it, and what was of it gathered round and did not have length, and was bloody or like mud color, or black, or had no sensation; then it is necessary to avoid cutting it.
So there is a danger to the patient, so it is necessary if you see it in the description that was mentioned from its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit at the foot of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument whose description has been presented, then insert the probe into the grape.
And pull it down and cut it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in cutting the tonsils, and it is necessary that you do not cut from it except what exceeded the natural order without addition because if you cut from it more, it will harm the voice and speech.
Then after the cut, you use what we described in cutting the tonsils and treat it until it heals. If the patient is afraid of being cut, it is necessary to use the trick in treating it without fear or concern, and the face of treatment for it is with the sharp medicine, which is to place the head of the patient in his rock.
Then you press his tongue with the instrument that we mentioned, then take from the sharp water that I mentioned in the chapter on treatment, and knead it into a dough that is not extinguished, and make it neither thick nor thin, and fill it into the cavity of this instrument and this is its image:.
The side on which you place the medicine should be hollowed out like a spoon, and the instrument with the medicine is placed on the same spot, and the patient lies on his side so that saliva may flow from him from inside his throat so that nothing may go down his throat to harm him.
Then you hold your hand with the medicine and squeeze it on the spot for half an hour until you see that it has darkened and the pain of the medicine subsided. And if you wish to take cotton, you wrap it around the tip of the mrod and moisten the cotton in the medicine.
And you insert the mrod with cotton into a tube from above until the cotton adheres to the spot. Do this repeatedly until you reach what you want of the amount of the grape then leave it, for it will shrivel and fall off after three or four days. If you need to apply the medicine again, reapply it.
After the application, you wipe around the grape with cotton moistened in butter and dry the surrounding area of medicine. Then, gargle with cold water and treat it from the outside with poultices and from the inside with gargles until it heals. This type of treatment is safer than cutting and further away from fear.
And the spot can also be treated with something milder than applying a poultice or cutting. It is treated with incense in this manner:  Take a handful of frankincense, saffron, spikenard, thyme, rue, lavender, chamomile, and similar herbs. Gather them all together or some of them in a pot and immerse them in vinegar.
And it is boiled with the pot covered with clay, and there is a hole in the center of the lid. On top of this, you place the  smoothed instrument made of silver or copper:
And you insert the end containing the incense into the mouth of the patient until the steam rises to the spot through the tube until the spot is well covered. Then, repeat it several times until it shrivels. Beware that you do not make this treatment at the first occurrence of the swelling.
For indeed it often increases the swelling, and this should be done only when the heat of the tumor subsides. If you do not have this tool, take a splint and fix on its end a piece of eggshell so that the patient's mouth does not burn.
For the eggshell prevents the heat of the steam from burning the mouth, and this is good treatment with safety.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
On extracting thorns and anything else that grows in the throat.
Often a bone or thorn of fish, or something else grows in the throat, and it is necessary to extract what is visible to the eye after pressing the tongue with the instrument at the sun.
So that what is in the throat becomes clear to you, and if it does not appear to you and it is hidden in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit before he swallows his food into his stomach, for perhaps the thing growing will come out with the vomit, or the patient may swallow a piece of bread or even a root.
Or he may swallow a piece of dry bread, or take a piece of soft sea sponge and tie it to a thread, then have him swallow it, and when it reaches the place of the thorn, pull the thread quickly. Do this several times.
For often the thorn or bone will stick to it and be brought out, and if it does not come out by what has been mentioned, then use a tool of lead in this form: .
It should be thicker than the reed a little, and at its end there is an eye that the patient inserts into his throat gently while he raises his head upward and takes care not to touch his larynx so as not to cause him to cough, and drives out the bone or thorn, or the physician inserts it with his hand.
And inserting the patient into it is better because he knows the position of the thing growing and pushes down or pulls up with his hand on the tool, all according to what appears appropriate for him until it comes out.
The Ninth and Thirty-First Chapter
On extracting the lodged phlegm in the throat.
If you have treated the phlegm with what has been mentioned in the division of treatment with medicines and it did not benefit, then look at the throat of the sick person in the sunlight after pressing his tongue with the instrument that has been described to you.
If your sight falls upon the phlegm, draw it out with a small fishing hook or a soft but firm thread; if you are unable to do so, then take a hollow tube and insert it into the throat of the sick person near the phlegm, then insert inside the tube an iron rod protected by fire.
Do this several times and have the sick person abstain from water throughout the day, then he should take a cup filled with cold water and open his mouth into it, gargling with it without swallowing a drop, and moving the water with his hand every so often.
If the phlegm falls into place if it feels the water, if it does not come out with what has been described, then vaporize the throat with urine and boiled water using the instrument that has been described in the incense section, do this several times as it will fall.
And the method of working with incense is to take a pot containing hot embers and cover it with a lid in the middle of which there is a hole; mount the tip of the instrument in that hole, then throw the incense, and have the sick person place his mouth on the end of the tube and close his mouth so that the incense does not come out until he feels that the incense has reached his throat.
If the phlegm falls into place, if it does not fall, then repeat the incense several times and have the sick person endure thirst and eat salt and garlic without drinking water, there is no doubt that it will come out with this method, and this is a picture of an instrument used to attract the phlegm from the throat when it comes into sight.
It is like a forceps, except it has this loop that goes into the throat and its ends resemble the beak of a bird; inside it has a roughness like that of an instrument for scraping, if you press it on something, it does not let go.
There is another instrument with which you press down on the tongue, it is a wide ring of iron as wide as the mouth, placed above the tongue and put into the mouth standing on its side; so that the mouth remains open involuntarily and the patient cannot remove it at all until it is removed.
Description of the instrument used to open the mouth in this same way.
Chapter Forty.
Here he will discuss tumors and their incision.
Tumors come in many different varieties, each discussed individually in this book.  They differ in their incision and opening, from two perspectives: one related to the nature of the tumor itself and its contents,
and the second perspective from the location where they occur in the body because a tumor that occurs in the head is different from a tumor that occurs in the buttock, and a tumor that occurs in the region of flesh is different from a tumor that occurs in a joint; each one of these has its own rules for treatment.
And some tumors should not be opened until the pus within them has ripened and matured, and some should be opened before they have fully ripened, like those that are near joints.
Because if a tumor occurs near a joint and its duration is prolonged until it decays surrounding tissues, it may damage the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing paralysis of that limb, or the tumor may be near a vital organ.
Because if you delay its opening until it matures, it may harm that vital organ, or it may be near the buttock, so you open it before it is fully ripe; however, it is necessary to open a tumor that is not fully ripe and near the buttock, lest it decay, penetrate into the anus, and become gangrenous.
It becomes in a place that does not heal, and it behooves you to learn the time of cutting tumors which have ripened completely, and this is when calmness of the tumor's pain and disappearance of fever and decrease of redness and pulsation and softening of the head of the tumor and all its signs.
It behooves you to place the cut at the bottom of the tumor's location if it is possible so that it is easier for the fluid to flow downwards or in the softer location of the tumor and the most protruding one, and let the cut go in the length of the body if the tumors are in the hands or feet.
And places of muscles and tendons and nerves and arteries and in general all places that are flat and have no bending, as for those that bend let the cut go according to that place, and as for if the tumor is in fleshy places it is best to leave it uncut.
Until it reaches full ripeness as we have said, if you cut it before that the discharge from it would be long and very harmful and filthy and perhaps its edges would harden and close up, and some tumors may be cut across the body when necessary or according to what the limb needs.
It behooves you to use one cut in small tumors and a wide cut or many incisions according to the size of the tumor in large ones, and there may be some tumors that need the skin to be stitched and cut if it has become like cloth.
And it becomes in a place that has died like what is shown in many moles and abscesses, some of them are cut with a three-angled incision and some are cut from it like the shape of an Arabic mulberry leaf.
And some of them use the circular incision and the crescent-shaped incision and similar incisions, and if it has no head like smooth flattened tumors it behooves you to cut it with a simple cut only, and it behooves you if the tumor is large and has gathered much fluid and cut it not to hasten to remove all of the pus at that time.
Then extract some of it and tighten the tumor for another day, then extract some more pus also, do this repeatedly gradually until all is extracted.
Especially if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an old man, for the animal spirit often dissolves with the discharge of pus in one go, so perhaps the patient may die and you will not feel it, therefore beware this chapter with utmost caution.
And after you have cut these tumors, it is necessary to wipe the wound and look. If the tumor's wound is small or the incision was one simple one, use cotton wool or lint made of linen. And if the tumor was large and the incisions from cutting were many.
Then it is necessary to put a thread in each incision until some of them reach each other, and if the tumor had some of its skin cut or hardened, then it is necessary to pack it with lint or fine linen without moisture and tighten it on the third day.
Then remove it and treat it as necessary with ointments until it heals, and if bleeding occurs during your work, use cold water and vinegar after you have soaked a linen cloth in them and hold it on the bleeding site repeatedly.
And if the bleeding persists, it is necessary to use the measures, treatment and remedies that we described in many places in this book of ours and in the classification, and if you are in wintertime and the tumor's location is rich in nerves, then it is necessary to moisten the bandages with a hot drink and oil.
And place them on the location, and if you are in summer and the locations were fleshy, then it is necessary to hold the bandages soaked in water and oil or with a drink and oil all cold until when the third day as we said, it is necessary to remove the tumor and wipe it.
And use in its treatment what resembles it until it heals, this is all you need to know about the treatment of tumors in general and as for the way of detailing, I have mentioned each tumor how to treat it described and summarized.
Chapter Forty-One
On the incision for tumors that appear in the skin of the head.
On the skin of the head tumors appear, small in size and among the kinds of growths it contains are cysts which have conditions such as a hen’s eggshell, and their types are many; some are fatty and others contain moisture like mud.
And some contain moisture like broth and soup, and others are hardened solid; all of them pose no danger in incision and removal unless you encounter a vein when cutting into them.
And the work in cutting into them is to first scrape them with the instrument whose image comes after this one, called the “meds,” until you know what they contain. If what they contain is moisture, then cut it lengthwise with a simple incision as shown in this image:
Begin the incision from line ~B~ to line ~J~. If the moisture empties, then remove the sac that contained it and cut all of it entirely; leave nothing of it whatsoever because often it returns if something is left.
Then immerse cotton in the salve if it is present, otherwise in salt water, and fill the wound with it, and leave it for a day; because it consumes what remains of the sac. Then reapply the cotton with the salve again and again as needed.
Until you are certain that nothing remains of the sac, then treat the wound with salves until it heals. If the tumor contains fatty substance, cut into it as shown in this image:
A crosswise incision and the pliers in the edge of the wound, and remove it from all sides, and exert effort to extract the sac that contains it. If you encounter a vein, do what was described earlier, and do the same for the tumor if it is hardened upon incision.
The treatment of a tumor, as I have mentioned, and the incision into a hardened tumor is easier because it contains little blood and moisture. And it may happen that some tumors in the head of some people contain no moisture at all.  For instance, when I incised a tumor....
The head of an old woman, when I incised it, the tumor was like a solid rock, rough and white; no one could break it, even if they threw it at it with force. And none of the other tumors that occur in the head are like this, except for those that appear on the heads of children.
And when it is at the root of the ears, make a simple incision into it all and make its bottom from its lower side so that the material flows easily downwards, then treat it with what suits it from treatment.
Chapter Forty-Two.
In the incision into tumors that appear in the neck, these tumors often appear in the neck and under the armpits and in the groins. And they may appear in all parts of the body.  And what appears in the neck from them may be one, or it may be many, and some of them are generated from others.
And each tumor of them is within a special peritoneum, as in the abscesses and tumors of the head as we have described. And there are many kinds of these tumors; some are hardened, some contain moisture, and some are malignant and do not respond to treatment.
And I have not seen any of them that were good in feeling, and whose appearance was close to the color of the skin, moving in every direction, and it was not attached to the nerves of the neck or to the fascia or artery, nor was it sunken. So it is necessary to incise it with a simple incision from the top to the bottom of the body, along this shape from line ~a~ to line ~b~.
And peel it from every side and extend the lips of the skin with a stitch or two stitches or many stitches, if you need that, as we have said in tumors of the head, and bring it out little by little so that it is on a neck not to cut any artery or nerve. And let the scalpel be not too sharp.
Lest your hand increase the severance or trouble the sick person, cut what does not need to be cut; if you have severed an artery or a vein and it has deprived you of work, put in the wound ground saffron or some fragments that stop bleeding.
Tighten the wound and leave it until the swelling subsides and the wound relaxes and begins to heal; for when the blood stops then return to your work until you are finished, then examine with your index finger if any remnants remain, then small clots, cut them and clean them out.
If there is a large artery at the base of the clot, it is necessary that you do not cut this clot from its base but rather tie it with a doubled strong thread and leave it until it falls off by itself without harm, then pack the wound with clean cotton that has been soaked in Egyptian ointment and then treat it.
And if you have cut the clot entirely, it is necessary that you bring the edges of the wound together and stitch it an hour after that, provided that you know that there is no remaining fragment of the clot; if you see that there remains a fragment due to the size of the clot.
It is necessary that you aim for the base and origin of it with cutting and use stitching as we have mentioned, and whatever of the clots contain moisture pack them with a simple pad where you see the place of ripening and make the pad as below as we said.
Then after the pad, use a layer of Egyptian ointment and its like for it to consume what remains of the decay until if you see the wound has cleaned itself, treat it with ointments that are good for flesh until it heals.
Chapter Forty-Third.
In the incision of the larynx about a tumor that arises inside the throat.
The ancients mentioned this incision in the larynx, and I have not seen anyone in our country perform it; this is the order of their words. As for those who suffer from angina pectoris, they should avoid cutting the larynx as they do not benefit from it.
In order that all the vocal cords and the lung be sound, but if they have a hot tumor in the mouth or throat or tonsils and there is no ailment in the trachea, it is necessary to use an incision of the larynx to escape from the defect which comes from choking.
Where we desire that, it is necessary to make an incision of the larynx below three circles from the circles of the trachea or four small incisions lengthwise between two circles as much as the incision in the peritoneum and not in the cartilage, and this position is suitable for the incision.
Because it is devoid of flesh and blood vessels are distant from it, if the surgeon is cowardly, it is necessary to extend the skin of the throat with a string then he incisions the skin until when it arrives at the trachea beside blood vessels if he sees something from them.
Then he incisions the peritoneum that we described, and he infers about the incision of the trachea from the phlegm that comes out from it with what is torn and from the interruption of the voice and leave the wound open for a time then when the time which was feared by choking passes gather the lips of the wound from the skin.
And its plan alone without the cartilage, then medicinal herbs are used that sprout flesh until it heals, said the author of this book, an explanation of the meaning of this speech which we have narrated is if they saw the patient had choked one of these tumors they mentioned.
And the patient is in danger of death and his soul was about to depart, they went to incision of the larynx so that the patient could breathe on the place of the wound some breathing and be delivered from death, but they were commanded to leave the wound open until the end of the disease and its course for three days or so.
Then they commanded to sew the wound and treat it until it heals, and what I saw with my own eyes that a servant took a dagger and sent it on her throat and cut some of the trachea from her lung so she was called to be treated and found her rotting as a slaughtered animal, so I uncovered the wound.
I found the blood that came out of the wound to be flowing easily, so I realized that she had not severed an artery or vein.  Air was coming out of the wound, so I plugged it and sutured the wound and treated it until he recovered, and nothing happened to the patient except for a little pain in his voice no more.
And she returned after some days to her best condition, so from here we say that a cut in the larynx is not dangerous.
Chapter Forty-Four.
In the incision on the tumor that appears in the pharynx from outside and is called a pharyngeal fistula.
This tumor which is called a pharyngeal fistula is a large tumor on the color of the body and it is common in women and it is of two kinds.
Either it is natural or it is acquired, as for the natural one there is no cure for it and as for the acquired one it is of two kinds, one resembling fatty tumors and the other resembling a tumor that comes from the complication of the artery and in its incision there is danger. So it is not appropriate to expose her to the iron at all except if she was small, if you probe and examine her with a probe, and find that she resembles a fatty tumor and was not attached to anything from the arteries, then cut her as you cut fatty tumors. And remove her with what contains it from the cyst if she is in a cyst, otherwise, explore all of it and then treat the place with the appropriate treatment.
Chapter Forty-Five.
In the incision on kinds of tumors.
Tumors are of many types and I have mentioned all their kinds in the classification, and it is necessary to tell here the difference between a tumor and an abscess because it is a problem, so I say that an abscess comes with heat, fever, and painful pains until the boiling of the boil subsides. And the suppuration is completed, and at that time the fever and the sharpness subside, and there are no heat or fever or pain with it, and it contains a serous sac which is a special covering for it, and it is on the color of the body, and its beginning is like lentils, and it becomes like a pancake and larger and smaller.
And it is of two kinds, either fatty or that it contains moisture, and the colors of the moisture are many as mentioned in the classification, so if you reach to treat the suppuration, it must be dried and searched first with the instrument called the probe as its image comes in the chapter after this.
Estimate the size of the tumor, then remove the probe and look at what comes out after it. If a flowing moisture of any color comes out, then cut it with a simple incision as mentioned in all tumors. If no moisture comes out after the probe, know that it is fatty.
So make an incision on it with a crossed incision like I taught you, and suspend it with the pins and peel the skin from every side gently, and take care of the sac if you can extract it whole with the suppuration.
If the sac ruptures while working and you could not extract it whole, which happens often, then take it out piece by piece until nothing remains of it, because if something remains, whether little or much, the suppuration will most likely return.
If you are overcome and a little remains, then shave the wound when it is empty with some sharp pointy tools and tighten the wound, and put something on top that soothes the hot tumor and treat it with all other treatments until it heals. If the suppuration is large, outline its edge and treat it with what promotes healing.
If a striking or non-striking sweat crosses you and there is bleeding, act quickly. Shave the place with powdered saffron and leave it tightened for two or three days until the wound suppurates and the boiling of blood subsides, then return to cutting what remains of the suppuration.
Chapter Six and Forty
In Images of Instruments.
Of those which are used in incisions and cavities, there are images of probes, which come in three types: large, medium, and small.

The Ninth and Fortieth Chapter.
In the incision of a tumor that appears in front of an artery or vein, called aneurism.

And the one that is from the vein, the tumor will be round in the outer part of the body; and the incision on these tumors is dangerous, especially what is in the armpit, collarbone, neck, and many places in the body if it was very large, so it is necessary to avoid treating them with iron.
And what was from them also in the limbs or head, it is necessary to avoid; and whatever was from swelling of the artery, then make a lengthwise incision on the skin above it, then open the incision with forceps, then dissect the artery and free it from its coverings.

And the tumor resolves, then you use the treatment that produces pus until the ligatures fall off, then treat it with ointments suitable for it until it heals.

The Fiftyeth Chapter.
In the swelling that results from nerve twisting.
Just as a swelling appears in the artery and vein, so too does it appear in the nerve if it is struck or from excessive strain or the like, and this is more common in the wrists and heels.
And in every place where the joints move, it is a hard swelling that resembles the color of the rest of the body, and it is mostly without pain. If it is pressed tightly, the patient feels a sensation similar to numbness, and the swelling is not gathered deep within the body.
But it is under the skin, and it moves in every direction, and does not go forward or backward. So what is like this in the joints should not be treated with iron, because it may cause a time of harm, and what is like this in the head or forehead.
So, cut the skin with a scalpel. If the swelling is small, grasp it with forceps and cut it from its root. If it is large, tie it with a bandage and remove it, then close the wound with stitches and treat it until it heals.
The Sixty-First Chapter.
In the cutting of warts that appear in the abdomen.
Many people often get boils in their stomachs and throughout their bodies, called "fistulae" because they resemble a fissure. Their origin is soft and their head is thick, sometimes their lips transform, some are small and others very large indeed.
I once saw a man with two boils in his stomach, resembling fissures; their origin was white and delicate, their lips had transformed and cracked, and fluid continuously flowed from them. I cut them open and threw each one onto the balance; one weighed about eighteen ounces, and the other about six.
And the procedure for cutting them is to look; if the patient is moist and the boil is white, wet, and delicate in origin, then cut it with a wide scalpel, and let your assistants have hot coals ready by the fire, because very often much blood will rush forth when they are cut.
So if blood overcomes you, then cauterize it. And if you see the patient cowardly and frightened by the cutting with iron, take a thread of lead tightly wound and pull with it the boil which has this description, leaving it for two days, then increase the tightening of the lead; do not cease to tighten the lead.
Every time it affects the boil until it breaks off and falls from itself without pain, if the boil is thick in origin, there is some fear and danger in cutting it, especially if it is in the stomach, but it can be cut in half or part of it.
Then it is cauterized so that it does not return, and then treated until the wound heals. Be careful not to expose yourself to cutting a boil that is dark in color, with little feeling, coarse in appearance; for this is cancerous, and I will mention cancer after this.
Chapter Twenty-Five.
Treatment of a Growth on the Genitals.
A growth on the genitals may arise from many causes, either from a rupture of the peritoneum on the abdomen, out of which intestines or bowels may protrude as mentioned in other hernias, or from blood flowing from a vein or artery as previously discussed, or from gas that is trapped there.
If it is before the rupture of the peritoneum and the emergence of the hernia, then its color will be similar to the color of the body and it will be soft without pain and appears in a different position. And if it is after the emergence of the intestines, then its position will be with what we described more different. If you press it with your fingers, it disappears then returns and perhaps it is accompanied by a crackling sound and it becomes greatly enlarged upon entering the bath or during intense fatigue. If it is before moisture, then it will be soft.
It does not disappear if you press it with your hand nor does it increase or decrease. If it is before blood, then with these signs the tumor appears to black. If it is before new flesh, then the tumor will be deep, hard and remains at a fixed amount.
If it is before wind, then touching it will be soft, and the action in that is to look. If the source of the tumor is from the artery or vein or wind, then you should refrain from treating it because there is fear and danger as I informed you in the chapter where I mentioned tumors that occur from the artery and vein.
If the source of the tumor is from the intestines or hernia, then you should order the patient to hold himself and stand upright extended, then learn with the stylus around the entire tumor. Then order him to lie down before you on his back, then dig around the tumor with a wide scalpel at the location you learned with the stylus, then extend the center of the tumor upward with a large bandage and then tie the place of the cut with a strong thread or silk cord tightly.
And the knot of the bandage should be a loop, then open the center of the drawn tumor above the bandage and insert your index finger into it and ask for the intestines. If you find that the bandage has taken it, loosen the loop and push the intestines back into the abdomen, and if you find a hernia, extend it with a bandage.
Cut the excess, and if a vein or artery obstructs you, tie it well and return to your work. Take two needles and insert two strong threads into them. Insert the needles into the incision you made around the tumor, fastening them there. Then pull the tumor in four places on the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave the place until the tightened flesh rots and falls off itself or cut it if it softens and rots, then treat it with the appropriate ointments until it heals. If the growth of the tumor is from flesh that has sprouted within it.
Or if it is from moisture, it is necessary to cut the tumor as we have said and remove the blood or moisture that you find there, then treat it with what mends the place.

The incision should be along the same line as the stone and your finger is placed in the anus while you press it outwards forcibly so that the incision is wide on the outside and narrow on the inside, as much as possible for the stone to exit.
Perhaps the finger in the anus will press out the stone when making the incision so it exits without difficulty, and know that there may be parts of a stone with angles and shapes which make it difficult to exit.
And some are smooth, like a plum, and rounded, making it easy for them to exit. So whatever of them has angles and shapes, increase the incision slightly. If it does not exit this way, it is necessary that you devise a way around it, either by grasping it with a forceps with a sharp, blade-like tip.
To hold onto the stone so it does not escape, or you may insert an instrument underneath it, with a blunt tip, and if you cannot manage this, widen the incision slightly. If you are overcome by some blood, cut it off with the saffron.
If there are more than one, push the largest first into the mouth of the bladder, then make an incision on it, and then push the smaller ones after that, and you should do the same if there are more than two. If they are very large, it is unwise to make a huge incision on them because this exposes the patient to two things.
Either he will die, or there will always be a trickle of urine because the place will not heal properly. But try to push them until they exit, or devise a way to break them with forceps so you can remove them completely.
If you have finished your work, wash the wound with vinegar and patience and apply a dressing to it, then place a cloth on top soaked in oil or syrup, or rose butter and cold water so that the hot swelling subsides, then the patient lies on his back and the bandage is not removed until the third day.
If it unravels, the place will be filled with much water and oil then treat it with palm ointment and basilik ointment until it heals. If a hot, excessive swelling appears in the wound, along with pus and the like, such as when blood clots in the bladder and urine is obstructed, and this is known by the presence of blood in the urine.
Then insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it indicates corruption of the bladder and its outflow. Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt and treat each type according to its kind until it heals.
In all times of treatment, it is necessary to tie the thighs together and bring them close to secure the medicines that are placed on the area. If the stone is small and has become in the urethra and lodged there, obstructing the urine from exiting, treat it with what I have described before it reaches the incision.
Therefore, often this treatment replaced the incision; I have tried it which is to take a probe made of steel, and its image is:
Triangular at the tip, sharp and inserted into a rod, then take a thread and tie it to the penis below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder, and gently insert the probe into the urethra until the probe reaches the stone itself.
And turn the probe in the stone a little at a time as you try to pierce it until it passes through from the other side, for then urine will flow and you close your hand on what remains of the stone from outside the penis, and it breaks apart and comes out with the urine, and the ailment heals.
If this treatment does not become feasible for you due to an obstacle that prevents it, then tie a thread below the stone and another thread above the stone, then make an incision on the stone within the penis between the two ties, and then remove it.
Then the bandage is applied and the clotted blood that has gathered in the wound is removed. The suture should be tied below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder, and the other suture above it so that when the suture is released after the removal of the stone, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound.
Therefore, when you tie the upper suture, you should raise the skin above so that it returns when you finish and covers the wound as we have said.
Chapter Sixty-One.
On Removing Stones from Women.
Stones are rarely produced in women, if a woman happens to have one it is difficult to treat and prohibited for many reasons. One reason is that the woman may be a virgin, and the second is that you cannot find a woman who allows herself to the physician.
If she is a virgin or belongs to those who are forbidden, and the third is that you cannot find a woman skilled in this craft, especially working with her hands, and the fourth is that the location of the incision on the stone in women is far from the location of the stone, so it needs a deep incision.
And in this danger, if necessity demands it, then a skilled female physician must be taken, and such are rarely found. If she is unavailable, then seek a chaste male physician or bring in an experienced midwife who is knowledgeable about women's affairs, or a woman who has some knowledge of this craft.
Bring her in and instruct her to do everything you command her, starting with examining the stone. First, she should examine whether the woman is a virgin. If so, she should insert her finger into her vagina and examine the stone, and if found, press it under her finger.
Then, command her to make the incision on her. If she is not a virgin but has given birth, order the midwife to insert her finger into the vagina of the woman and examine the stone after placing her left hand on the bladder and pressing it firmly.
If you find it, it is necessary to place it from the mouth of the bladder downwards to the extent of its capacity until it reaches the root of the thigh, then make an incision on it opposite the middle of the groin at the root of the thigh from whichever side it appears to you and you feel the stone in that area.
And your finger should not remove from the stone, pressing under it, and let the incision be small at first, then you insert the probe on that small incision, if you feel the stone, increase in the incision to the extent that you know the stone will exit from it, and know that there are many types of stones.
Some are small and large, smooth and rough, long and round, and with branches, so know their types so that you may deduce what you want. If blood overcomes you, throw in the place a pinch of powdered saffron and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops, then return to your work.
Until the stone exits, and do that you may count within yourself from the instruments mentioned in extracting stones from men to assist you in your work, if excessive bleeding overcomes you and you know by the pulse of blood that it is from a severed artery, place the cauterizer on the location.
And tighten it with the cauterizer tightly and leave it, do not touch it and leave the stone, so perhaps the illness will perish, then treat the wound, if the sharpness of blood subsides after days and the place cleanses, return to your work until the stone exits.
Chapter Sixty-Second.

Chapter Thirty-Sixth.
On the incision on the fleshy groin and its treatment.
Know that the incision on this fleshy groin is a grave danger leading to destruction in most cases, so we see it left and safety sought from it, and I am mentioning the work in it and types of swelling.

Chapter Forty-Sixth.

The Fifth Sixth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Fistulas in the Intestines.
The occurrence of this fistula is from a fissure that appears in the peritoneum extending on the abdomen toward the flanks from the bottom side of the belly, so the intestines protrude through this opening into one of the ovaries.
And this hernia is either from a fissure in the peritoneum or from its stretching, and these two types occur from many causes: either a blow or a kick or a shout or lifting something heavy and similar. Its sign is that if it is from the stretching of the peritoneum, it occurs gradually over a long period of time.
And it does not occur suddenly and the swelling is level to about the depth before the peritoneum compresses the intestines, and its sign is that if it is from a fissure in the peritoneum, it occurs from the very beginning with severe pain all at once and the swelling appears visibly under the skin nearby.
This is due to the intestine coming out and its path going outside of the peritoneum, and it may come out with the hernia, called this hernia intestinal and hernial. And it may be with wind, and it may run in the intestine feces and it becomes trapped there, so that death comes with the patient.
Because it causes severe pain and crackling, especially if pressed, and treatment of these kinds of diseases with iron is dangerous so you should be careful not to fall into it. The method is that you order the patient to return the intestine with his hand inside his belly if it comes back.
Then he lies on his back between your hands and raises his legs, then you stretch the skin following the hernia above and cut all the scrotum skin lengthwise, then you insert forceps into the edge of the incision as much as needed to open the incision with them.

Chapter seventy-seventh.
On hernias that occur in the groin.
A hernia in the groin may occur as we have mentioned, where the contents do not protrude and nothing from the intestines descends; but if it does descend, it is easy to return at all times.
But if it lasts for a long time, the opening in the peritoneum increases until the intestines and the omentum descend into the scrotum, which occurs due to the extension of the peritoneum in the groin as we have mentioned. This is because the peritoneum extends then relaxes and pushes the contents, and it is treated with a ligature as I have previously described.
It can also be treated with iron in this way: the patient lies on his back between your hands, then you make an incision at the site of the hernia which is warm, a lengthwise incision about three finger widths long, and then you smooth out the peritoneum beneath the skin.
Until the white peritoneum beneath it is exposed, then you take a ligature and place it on the spot arising from the peritoneum, pressing it into the depths of the abdomen, then stitch the two areas together at the end of the ligature on the peritoneum, and glue them together with stitching.
Then you pull the end of the ligature and do not cut the peritoneum at all, nor touch the testicle or anything else as I have taught you in treating intestinal hernias, then treat it with surgical treatment.
If the sutures are cut, clean them and bandage the wound until it heals; the peritoneum contracts and does not increase the protrusion of the hernia.
And a ligature is better in this place because it is closer to safety.
The eighth and sixty chapter.
On relaxation of the scrotum skin.
The skin of the scrotum often relaxes in some people, without relaxing the flesh inside it, and its appearance is unsightly.  So for those who desire to treat it, he should put the patient on his back.
And cut all the skin that has relaxed on the thick skin, then bring the lips together, and if you wish, first stitch the excess loose skin with three or four stitches and make sure of the stitching, then cut what is between the stitches.
Then treat it with the treatment of all other wounds until it heals and the sutures fall out.
Chapter ninety-six.
On castration.
Castration in our religion is forbidden.
And for this reason it was incumbent upon me not to mention it in this book of mine, but I have mentioned it for two reasons: one is that it should be known to the physician if he is asked about it and that he may know the treatment of those who have undergone it, and the other reason is that we often need to castrate some animals for our benefit.
Such as sheep, goats, cats, and the like of animals. I say that castration is done in two ways: either by softening or by cutting and severing. The one done by softening is that we put the animal in hot water until its testicles relax and soften and hang down.
Then soften it with your hand until it dissolves and is not discernible to the touch. As for castration by cutting and severing, it is necessary to hold the animal and squeeze its scrotum with the left hand, then tie the cords and cut a single incision on each testicle.
Until when the two testicles protrude, cut them after stripping them and leave nothing on them but the thin peritoneum that is on the vessels. This type of castration is better than the one done by softening.
Because softening may leave something of the testicles, and the animal may then desire mating. Then the wound is treated until it heals.
Chapter seventy.
In the treatment of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men appears in two types: one is that which appears below the space or in the scrotum skin between women, shaped like a woman's genitals with hair and perhaps urine flows from what is in the scrotum skin.
As for women, there is one type and it appears above the genitals on the pubis like a small male member protruding outward, one resembling the male penis and the two resemble female genitalia, and the treatment of the three types.
The two types from men and the single type from women should have that excess flesh cut until its trace is erased, then treated with the treatment of all surgeries until it heals. As for the second type of man who urinates from what is in the scrotum skin, there is no work to be done and the protrusion does not heal.
Chapter Seventy-One.
In cutting the clitoris and flesh protruding from women's genitals.
The clitoris may increase in amount beyond the natural order until it becomes prominent and spoils its appearance, and it may grow large in some women until it spreads like that of men and becomes fit for intercourse.
It is necessary to grasp the excess of the clitoris with your hand or a clamp and cut it, without being excessive in cutting, especially in the depth of its root lest it cause bleeding.
Then treat it with the treatment of surgeries until it heals. As for the protruding flesh, it is flesh that grows in the mouth of the womb until it fills it.
And perhaps it protrudes outside like the tailbone. Therefore, some of the ancients call it the "tailbone disease," so it should be cut like the clitoris and treated until it heals.
Chapter Seventy-Two.
In the Treatment of Dislocation.
Dislocation is when a woman's vagina is not pierced or the opening is small, and it can be either natural, present at birth, or acquired, which occurs due to an advanced cause that was previously mentioned, and this can be from excessive flesh growth.
or thin or thick peritoneum and it can be in the depth of the womb or its sides or above or below it, preventing intercourse, the umbilical cord, and childbirth, and possibly menstruation. This is known by examining it with a midwife.
If the obstruction is apparent and nearby, if it isn't apparent then examine it with her fingers or a probe. If the obstruction is from thin peritoneum and close to the vulva, immediately try to rupture it, which means placing on the vulva a semblance of a  spoon then place your thumbs from both hands together.
And the woman on her back with legs spread apart, then extend the vulva forcefully until the thin peritoneum ruptures and the obstruction opens, then take a cloth dipped in oil and place it on the area and have intercourse with the woman every day so that the area doesn't close again.
If the peritoneum is thick and dense, it's necessary to cut it with a wide scalpel resembling a piece of paper. If the obstruction is from excessive flesh, cauterize it with forceps, cut it, and have medications that stop bleeding without a sting on hand, such as mastic, frankincense, and myrrh mixed with egg white.
Then use a wide lead pipe so the wound doesn't close quickly, hold it for days, and use a dry cotton swab. Then treat it with all the treatments for scar tissue until it heals. Sometimes there may be another flesh growth in the womb, which should be cut in this way.
Unless it's a cancerous tumor, a tumor in the womb should not be treated with iron at all.
Chapter thirty-seven.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids and warts and red boils that appear in the vulva of women.

It is best that the woman enters a cold house, then stretches the warts with a file or a rough linen cloth and cuts them from their roots, then she puts on them when blood flows from one of the points that cut the blood without cauterization.
Like frankincense, mastic, myrrh, and the like, then she raises her legs to the wall for an hour, then lowers them into cold water. If the bleeding persists, make her sit in a decoction of tamarind, pomegranate peel, grape seed, etc., then take barley flour and knead it with honey and vinegar.
And apply it on her back, if the blood stops, otherwise, bind the chest and the breasts without condition. Then take a poultice and soak it in the juice of pomegranate,  or the juice of ass's hoof or the juice of rue branches with grape seed syrup and apply it to the area.
If the swelling subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals. As for the red boil, it resembles a rough-looking bunch of thorns. It is necessary to cut what has appeared from it according to what I have mentioned in the case of warts and treat it until it heals.
Chapter thirty-eight.
In the matter of fistulas that appear in the uterus.
