Then tighten with another bandage above his hips and above his knees and at his ankle; then gather all the bandages together and tie them to the other plank at his feet; then each servant extends his plank towards his side with the bandage and the planks do not move from their fixed positions therein.
Unless they are not firmly secured as we mentioned, and the physician places his hands on the vertebra with force until it returns or places a board on top of it and leans on the board with his legs until it returns; if it does not return by this treatment, then take a board that is about three cubits long.
And dig in the wall that we mentioned to be near the patient a place where you insert the end of the board; then place the middle of the board on the vertebra and the physician places his legs on the other end and tightens it well until he compresses the vertebra.
And it returns to its place; and if you want to make it with the spiral that is tightened by hand, which is to insert two planks into the earth at the head of the patient at one end of the bench and two other planks at his feet at the other end of the bench.
And let it be after each plank a cubit, and make in each plank a hole through which the spiral runs and secure all the wood firmly in the earth well so that it does not move at all, and insert a round rod which is the spiral that winds around the bandage in the holes of the two planks.
On one side there is a hole that has been plugged with a stick, its length an inch, and in the other two pieces of wood there is a similar thing. Then the rope which was tightened at the chest of the patient is tied to the winding post at his head and the ropes which were tightened at his legs are tied to the winding post at his feet.
Then a servant stands by each winding post, twisting his hand with the tool which winds the post and the physician smooths the hump as we have mentioned before, and this is a picture of the winding post, the bedpan and the patient.
Then after the bedpan is returned and the position is level, it is necessary to carry the dried bandage with egg white then the mesh and put from above the bandage a splint of wood which its width be three fingers or so and its length be as much as takes the place of the hump.
And on some beads of good quality, then it is tied with the rope that is necessary and the patient uses mild food until he heals, if some of the lump remained in its place at the end of the healing, it is necessary to use the medicines that soften and make soft along with the use of the splint we described before for a long time.
And a sheet of lead may be used in that, and a lump may appear at the end of the vertebrae of the back so it is thought to be slipped, and this is an extra bone that has grown, so do not expose it to this treatment because maybe death occurs.
Chapter thirty-one.
In the Treatment of a Dislocated Hip.
Know that the hip joint and the shoulder joint are only subject to dislocation, not what other joints are subjected to from slight displacement and dislocation, and the hip joint dislocates in four directions.
That is to say, it dislocates inwards and outwards, forwards and backwards, and more often it dislocates inwards and less often it dislocates forwards or backwards, and the sign of its dislocation inwards is that if you compare the limb of the patient that is healthy with the diseased one, the latter will be longer.
The knee is more extended than usual and the patient cannot bend his leg at the hip, and the place below the hip is swollen and livid before the head of the femur has reached there.
And the sign of one whose jaw is displaced outwards are symptoms opposite to these, and the sign of one whose jaw is displaced forwards is that he extends his leg completely except that he cannot bend it without pain in the knee, and even if he attempts to walk, he cannot do so forward.
And he retains his urine and suffers from a pain in the hip, and when he walks, his foot rests on his heel, and the sign of one whose jaw is displaced backwards is that he cannot extend his knee nor can he bend it before bending his hip, and his leg is also shorter than the other.
And the hip is relaxed and the head of the femur is at the place of the lower back, as for the remedy for these types of dislocation, it is that if you look and find that the dislocation has been present for a long time with its patient and he did not try to remedy it and remained in its state, then there is no treatment whatsoever.
So it is not proper to subject him to treatment, but as for the one whose dislocation was recent and whatever type it may be of the four types of dislocation, hurry to that you twist the joint and stretch it inward and outward and move it right and left so perhaps...
it returns and did not need anything else from treatment, if it does not return like this, then it is necessary to prepare a strong servant to extend his leg from below either with his hands or with a rope tied on his leg above the knee, and another servant extends it from above.
that he puts his hands under his armpit, then pulls with a soft rope on the origin of the femur and another servant holds the end of the rope, a third one and his pull is either from the front from the side of the hip to the side of the clavicle or from behind towards the back.
They should be pulled at all of them once until the patient rises with his body from the ground and remains suspended, for this type of traction is a common type among the four types, and if the jaw returns as we have said, otherwise there must be special treatment for each type that I have mentioned.
As for its special treatment if the jaw is inside, it is necessary for the patient to lie on his healthy side, then a bandage is placed on the root of the thigh between the head of the thigh and the place below the rib.
Then the bandage is extended upwards from the side of the rib to the top of the body towards the collarbone, then another strong servant takes it with his arms, embraces the thick place of the upper thigh of the patient and extends outwards with a strong pull, so it returns to its place.
And this type is easier than all other types of treatment by which this limb returns, if it becomes difficult for you and it does not respond to entering this type of treatment at all, then it is necessary to tie both legs of the patient with a strong, soft bandage on the heels and knees.
And after each one of them, it should be four fingers' width apart and the patient's leg is extended more than the other by two fingers, then the patient is suspended from his head on a wooden beam in the house and its distance from the ground should be an arm's length.
Then you order a strong boy to embrace the root of the thigh and another boy hangs from the patient and pushes the boy embracing the thigh with force, so the joint returns to its place quickly. As for its special treatment if the jaw is outside.
Then it is necessary for the patient to lie on his back as we described in the one with the hump, and the bandage is tightened on his upper leg especially and on his chest, then one beam is placed at his feet and the other at his head, then an additional beam is placed in the middle of the bed firmly fixed.
He wraps a damp cloth around it so as not to injure the patient, and places wood between his thighs so that he does not drag down when stretched, then each assistant stretches on his side, and the physician adjusts the hip with his hands, if it responds to being returned.
Otherwise, place the board on him and press it as we mentioned in the ridge, except that it is necessary for the patient to be lying on his correct side, and if the dislocation is forward, it is necessary to stretch the leg of the patient once while he is in this description exactly on the anvil.
And the physician places the palm of his right hand on the afflicted rib, then presses it with the other hand, and at the same time makes the pressure extended downwards towards the knee, and if the dislocation is backward, it is not necessary to stretch the patient downwards.
And he is raised on the ground, but it is necessary for him to be placed on a solid thing, as well as from his hip and knee outwards according to what we mentioned from his position on the anvil, he is on his face and the bandages are tightened.
As we have said before, it is necessary to use the clamp with the board also on the place where the joint came out of, so if the return of the hip joint is complete as necessary and the sign of its return is not hidden from you, which is that you stretch the legs of the patient.
If you see them level and the patient grabs his leg and stretches it without difficulty, know that the member has returned as necessary, so at this time, compare the thighs and apply the bandage and tighten with a turban tightly so that the hip does not move in any direction.
And it is necessary for the patient to be in stillness for three or four days, then remove the bandage and bandage and compare the leg with the other, if you see them equal in size, know that the fracture has set, so release the patient to walk, and if you see anything of relaxation.
Then return and bandage it and tighten it according to the first tightening of yours and leave it also for three days then remove it and walk slowly on it for days until it strengthens, God willing.
The Second Thirty-Second Chapter.
In the Treatment of a Broken Patella.
The knee breaks in three directions, it breaks inwards, outwards, and downwards, that is to the rear, and it does not break forward from the patella. The sign of its fracture is to order the patient to press his leg against his thigh.
If it does not stick to the thigh, know that the knee is fractured. To set all sides of the fracture, have the patient sit seated with his legs stretched out if he is able, and have an assistant behind him to hold his middle and pull him slightly backwards, then you sit on his thighs.
And press your back to his face and make his leg between your legs, then grasp his knee with your hands and intertwine them between your fingers on his knee, then compress his sides of the knee with your hands forcefully and another assistant extends his leg until the knee returns to its place.
And the sign of its return is that you press the leg to the thigh in a soft and unforced manner, then bandage it and stick the leg to the thigh, then bind them all with a bandage for three or four days, then release them, and he should not use except for walking a little for days until it strengthens.
If it is difficult for you to return it as we have described, then use the strong traction with the bandages that I have described in the treatment of the hip until it returns.
The Third Thirty-Third Chapter.
In the Treatment of a Broken Heel.
The heel may be dislocated slightly or it may fracture completely, and its fracture is either inwards or outwards, and the sign of its fracture is to see the heel swollen and protruding in the direction to which it fractured.
As for treating its falling away, it is easy to restore it by gently stretching it with the hands and smoothing it until it returns. As for treating it if it has completely separated, it is necessary that the patient sits seated and a strong servant holds him from behind his back in the middle.
Then, you hold his foot from the top with your right hand and from below his ankle with your left hand, then pull the foot towards you with your right hand then with your left twice, then stretch it with your left and push the front of the foot with your right towards the leg without force.
Do this twice as we described, then push the front of the foot towards the leg on the third time while you pull the ankle, if it returns in one or two times in this way and you see the foot level, otherwise repeat the work on it for it will return.
If it doesn't return with what we described, then lay the patient on his back on the ground and insert a wedge into the earth firmly so that it falls between his thighs, and wrap it in a cloth so as not to hurt the patient, then have a servant hold his thigh.
Then another servant stretches the leg either with his hands or with a bandage tying it around the neck of the leg, then each servant stretches in the opposite direction of the other and the wedge standing between the patient's thighs holds it so that his body does not pull down during the stretching, then the physician sets the bone with his hands.
And another servant holds the healthy leg down, for the bone returns quickly, if the bone returns and it becomes clear to you that its return is correct, apply the bandage and splint and tighten them with strong bandages and tie the foot to the bottom with a bandage, and it is necessary to avoid the nerve that is above the heel from behind.
So that the bandage is not too tight on it and hurts him, then leave him for two or three days if the bandage relaxes tighten it again then release it on the third or fourth day, and the patient refrains from walking for forty days.
If someone desires to walk before this period, it is not safe for the jaw to break and be spoiled, and not accepted for treatment afterward. If a hot tumor appears to him, it is necessary to use what we have described in another place of treatment and poultice until it disappears.
Chapter Forty-Third.
In the Treatment of a Fracture of a Man's Fingers.
It is necessary to straighten what is fractured from it with gentle stretching without force, and this is not difficult but easy. If the fracture is in some of the bones of the heel, it is necessary that the patient put his foot on a level place on the ground.
Or on a board while he is standing like when walking, then you place your foot on what protrudes from those joints and then press down on it with your foot with force until it returns and you see that it has straightened and there is no protrusion in the location.
Then put under the sole of his foot a board that takes the whole foot, it has two ends then tighten it tightly and firmly for three days, then remove it and protect him from walking for many days until it strengthens and there is safety from returning God willing.
Chapter Fifty-Third.
In the Kinds of Fracture Which Is With a Wound or With a Break or Both Together.
When something like that happens and it is treated and healed, it often follows with death.
Therefore, it is not necessary to undertake the treatment of such a thing except by one who is skilled in the craft, long in experience, gentle, compassionate, cautious, not hasty or reckless, and that he should use at the beginning the medicines that subdue hot tumors only and soothe the patient.
To God's power except for what I hoped for his safety from harm with mild illness and you saw in him some hope, then return him to your protection in the first place before the hot tumor arises.
If the member returns to what I desired, use the means that soothes hot tumors and treat the wound with ointments suitable for it, drying ones. If the jawbone is fractured and splinters of bone are scattered, then remove them. And follow in that what was mentioned in simple diseases from what came before in their places.
And be diligent in your effort and purify yourself from entering the path of error, as I have previously instructed you. That is best for your sake and safest for your exposure, if God wills.
